The Distinction Between Will and Emotional States
Maturidi answers the objection of Iblis's will overriding God's will by distinguishing will from pleasure and anger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's will is not contradicted by Iblis's will, and how Maturidi distinguishes between will (irāda) and emotions like pleasure (riḍā) and anger (sukht).

Core Idea
Will is a condition for action; pleasure and anger are not.

The objection that Iblis's will overrides God's will seems powerful: if God wants obedience but Iblis wants disbelief, why does disbelief happen? Maturidi's answer hinges on a key distinction: will is not the same as pleasure or anger. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic and translation of the objection: Iblis's will appears more effective than God's.
Notice how the objector uses the prevalence of disbelief.
2
Identify the answer
Maturidi answers by appealing to pleasure, love, and anger, not will.
3
Understand the distinction
Will is a necessary condition for action, whereas pleasure/anger can exist without the action at that moment.
This disarms the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عورض بما كان كفر أكثر عباد الله بأن أراد إبليس، والله أراد منهم الطاعة، فصارت إرادة إبليس في ملك الله وسلطانه أبعد من إرادة الله . فأجاب بالرضا والمحبة والسخط، وقد بيّنا نحن الفصل بين الأمرين على أنه يكون فعل يرضى به المرء ويسخط من غير أن كان وقت فعله، ومحال ذلك في الإرادة؛ ثبت أنها شرط الفعل فيما يُظهر التعجيز إذ لا يخلو عنها عنه، لأنهما فعل المختار وأيضا إنا لا نقول بأن الله يحب من يعلم أنه لا يؤمن أو يرضى عنه ، يجبان بالفعل، فمن لا يفعل فالقول به بعيد ; وأما الإرادة فقد بيّنا . والله أعلم. والأصل في هذا، في المتعارف أن الفعل يخرج على إرادة أو غلبة أو غفلة. ثم الله سبحانه لا يجوز أن يوصف في فعل العبد بالغلبة أو بالغفلة ، ثبت أن كان بالإرادة والمعتزلة لا يثبتون الله معنى في الإرادة سوى كون العلم بعد أن لم يكن من غير ضرورة له ، وهذا المعنى هو في فعل كل من أهل العالم قائم، فلا وجه لإنكارهم على قولهم. وبالله العصمة. ثم قال : إرادة إبليس هي التمنى، ولو أراد العباد ما كفروا، والله يقدر على منعهم بالقهر . { قال الفقيه رحمه الله : { قلنا له: قد صدقت؛ والإرادة قد توجب الغلبة، والتمنى لا، فكيف غلب تمنى عدوه على إرادته؟ وقوله : يقدر ويقهر» ، وهذا النوع إنما هو أثر الحيرة والوحشة، ولا يجوز الإيمان بالقسر بوجه ثم قال : فإن قيل: هل رأيت حكيما يقدر على منع عبده عن أمر لا يريده ولا يمنعه؟ فعارض بالجبر . وذا خطأ، لأنه عندنا يريده ، وليس المنع من شرط ما يراد. ثم قال : فإنه يعد لوجهين لا يريده، ولا يجوز له المنع لضرب من التدبير .
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: إن كنت على الشاهد تُقدره فلا تجده إلا أن لا يقدر عليه أو هو لم يرد الفعل به. قال : ومنها ما يجب فيها المنع ; فدل أن المنع إن وجب وجب لعلة لا لعينه. وما يُذكر من العلة فإن كانت أو جبت الاضطرار، فهو الذي قيل : لا يقدر عليه، وإن كان لا يوجب، وقد يملك القهر لا بالتعدى، فهو لا يسعه عندنا، وهو خارج من العرف.
ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then [the opponent] objected with [the fact] that the disbelief of most of God's servants was because Iblis willed [it], and God willed obedience from them, so Iblis's will in God's dominion and authority became more far-reaching than God's will. So he answered with pleasure, love, and anger. And we have clarified the distinction between the two matters: that there is an action with which one is pleased and angered without it being at the time of the action, but that is impossible in the case of will. It is established that [will] is a condition for the action in what appears as [an expression of] incapacity, since [action] is not free of it because they are [both] the act of the free agent. Also, we do not say that God loves one whom He knows will not believe, or is pleased with him — they [pleasure and love] are inseparable from action, so regarding one who does not act, saying it [about him] is far[-fetched]. As for will, we have clarified it. And God knows best. The principle in this, in common usage, is that action proceeds from will, or coercion, or forgetfulness. Then God, exalted, cannot be described in the servant's action as coercion or forgetfulness. So it is established that it is by will. And the Mu'tazila do not affirm for God a meaning in will beyond knowledge without necessity after it was not, and this meaning is present in the action of every person in the world, so there is no basis for their denial of their own statement. And with God is protection. Then he said: Iblis's will is mere wish, and if the servants willed [faith] they would not disbelieve, and God has power to prevent them by compulsion. The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: We said to him: You have spoken truth; will necessitates coercion, but wish does not. So how did the wish of His enemy overcome His will? And his saying 'He has power and compels' — this type [of answer] is only the effect of confusion and alienation, and belief in compulsion is not permissible in any way. Then he said: If it is said: Do you see a wise man who has power to prevent his servant from a matter he does not will and does not prevent him? He objected with [the doctrine of] compulsion, and that is an error because according to us He wills it, and prevention is not a condition of what is willed. Then he said: He counts it for two aspects He does not will, and prevention is not permissible for Him due to some [aspect of] governance. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: If you were to measure by the witnessed, you would not find [such] except that he does not have power over it or he did not will the action. He said: Among [the cases] is that which necessitates prevention; so it indicates that if prevention is necessary, it is necessary for a cause, not for itself. What is mentioned of the cause, if it necessitated compulsion, then that is what was said: he does not have power over it. And if it does not necessitate, and he [the agent] may own compulsion without transgression, then it is not permissible for him according to us, and it is outside of custom. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a theological objection and its response regarding divine will and human action. The objector argues: most people disbelieve because Iblis willed it, yet God wills obedience from them. Thus Iblis's will appears more effective in God's own dominion. The author answers by distinguishing between will and emotions like pleasure and anger. A person can be pleased or angered without acting at that moment, but will is a condition for action; it must exist for the act to occur. Therefore, God does not love or have pleasure in the disbeliever as that would necessitate an action, whereas will is different. The author then states the common principle: action arises from will, coercion, or forgetfulness. God cannot be described by coercion or forgetfulness concerning the servant's act, so it must be by will. The Mu'tazila are criticized for not affirming a real attribute of will in God beyond a mere temporal knowledge without necessity. The text then presents a second objection: Iblis's will is mere wish (tamannī), not true will, because if the servants truly willed faith, they would not disbelieve. The jurist replies that will entails coercion (ghalaba), while wish does not, so how can the enemy's wish overcome God's will? Belief in compulsion (qahr) is rejected. A third objection asks: if a wise master can prevent his servant from an undesired act, why doesn't God do so? The opponent counters with compulsion, but this is wrong because God does will the act, and prevention is not required. The Shaykh explains that if one judges by human custom, prevention only occurs when the agent lacks power or does not will the act. Prevention, if necessary, must be for a cause, not arbitrarily. If the cause would lead to compulsion, then the agent truly lacks power; otherwise, compulsion is not permissible in divine governance. The passage concludes with a statement of reliance on God.

Key Terms
إرادة
الرضا
المحبة
السخط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's will is opposed by Iblis's will, so Iblis is independent.
Correction: Maturidi explains that will is a condition for action, and God's will always accompanies the act. Iblis's will does not override God's will; rather, God permits the act by His will.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes will (إرادة) from pleasure (رضا) and anger (سخط)?
A) Will is a condition for action, while pleasure and anger can exist without action at the moment.
B) Will is eternal, while pleasure and anger are temporal.
C) Will belongs only to God, while pleasure and anger belong to humans.
D) Will necessitates compulsion, while pleasure and anger do not.

Key Takeaway
Will is a necessary condition for action, while pleasure and anger are responses to action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see widespread disobedience in the world, do you ever feel that your will or the will of evil people is more powerful than God's will? How does today's lesson challenge that feeling and redirect your trust in God's sovereignty?
?
In your own struggles with sin, do you ever confuse God's permission (that He wills it to happen) with His approval? How can you apply Maturidi's distinction to separate what God allows for wisdom from what He loves?
?
Think of a person you know who persists in disbelief. Does your heart doubt God's power or justice? How does knowing that God's will is always effective—even while He does not love disbelief—change your perspective and your dua for them?

The Principle of Action and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Maturidi states the principle of action's origin and refutes the Mu'tazila on divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that action proceeds from will, coercion, or forgetfulness, and why God cannot be described by coercion or forgetfulness in the servant's act.

Core Idea
Action arises from will; God is free from coercion and forgetfulness.

Maturidi establishes a fundamental principle: every action originates from either will, coercion, or forgetfulness. Since God cannot be coerced or forgetful, every action in His creation occurs by His will. This lesson also addresses the Mu'tazila's denial of a real attribute of will in God.

Guided Path
1
Learn the three origins of action
Read the principle: action proceeds from will, coercion, or forgetfulness.
This is based on common usage.
2
Apply to God
God cannot be described by coercion or forgetfulness regarding the servant's action, so it must be by will.
3
Refute Mu'tazila
Mu'tazila deny a real attribute of will in God; their own view that will is knowledge without necessity is found in all human actions, so their denial is inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عورض بما كان كفر أكثر عباد الله بأن أراد إبليس، والله أراد منهم الطاعة، فصارت إرادة إبليس في ملك الله وسلطانه أبعد من إرادة الله . فأجاب بالرضا والمحبة والسخط، وقد بيّنا نحن الفصل بين الأمرين على أنه يكون فعل يرضى به المرء ويسخط من غير أن كان وقت فعله، ومحال ذلك في الإرادة؛ ثبت أنها شرط الفعل فيما يُظهر التعجيز إذ لا يخلو عنها عنه، لأنهما فعل المختار وأيضا إنا لا نقول بأن الله يحب من يعلم أنه لا يؤمن أو يرضى عنه ، يجبان بالفعل، فمن لا يفعل فالقول به بعيد ; وأما الإرادة فقد بيّنا . والله أعلم. والأصل في هذا، في المتعارف أن الفعل يخرج على إرادة أو غلبة أو غفلة. ثم الله سبحانه لا يجوز أن يوصف في فعل العبد بالغلبة أو بالغفلة ، ثبت أن كان بالإرادة والمعتزلة لا يثبتون الله معنى في الإرادة سوى كون العلم بعد أن لم يكن من غير ضرورة له ، وهذا المعنى هو في فعل كل من أهل العالم قائم، فلا وجه لإنكارهم على قولهم. وبالله العصمة. ثم قال : إرادة إبليس هي التمنى، ولو أراد العباد ما كفروا، والله يقدر على منعهم بالقهر . { قال الفقيه رحمه الله : { قلنا له: قد صدقت؛ والإرادة قد توجب الغلبة، والتمنى لا، فكيف غلب تمنى عدوه على إرادته؟ وقوله : يقدر ويقهر» ، وهذا النوع إنما هو أثر الحيرة والوحشة، ولا يجوز الإيمان بالقسر بوجه ثم قال : فإن قيل: هل رأيت حكيما يقدر على منع عبده عن أمر لا يريده ولا يمنعه؟ فعارض بالجبر . وذا خطأ، لأنه عندنا يريده ، وليس المنع من شرط ما يراد. ثم قال : فإنه يعد لوجهين لا يريده، ولا يجوز له المنع لضرب من التدبير .
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: إن كنت على الشاهد تُقدره فلا تجده إلا أن لا يقدر عليه أو هو لم يرد الفعل به. قال : ومنها ما يجب فيها المنع ; فدل أن المنع إن وجب وجب لعلة لا لعينه. وما يُذكر من العلة فإن كانت أو جبت الاضطرار، فهو الذي قيل : لا يقدر عليه، وإن كان لا يوجب، وقد يملك القهر لا بالتعدى، فهو لا يسعه عندنا، وهو خارج من العرف.
ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then [the opponent] objected with [the fact] that the disbelief of most of God's servants was because Iblis willed [it], and God willed obedience from them, so Iblis's will in God's dominion and authority became more far-reaching than God's will. So he answered with pleasure, love, and anger. And we have clarified the distinction between the two matters: that there is an action with which one is pleased and angered without it being at the time of the action, but that is impossible in the case of will. It is established that [will] is a condition for the action in what appears as [an expression of] incapacity, since [action] is not free of it because they are [both] the act of the free agent. Also, we do not say that God loves one whom He knows will not believe, or is pleased with him — they [pleasure and love] are inseparable from action, so regarding one who does not act, saying it [about him] is far[-fetched]. As for will, we have clarified it. And God knows best. The principle in this, in common usage, is that action proceeds from will, or coercion, or forgetfulness. Then God, exalted, cannot be described in the servant's action as coercion or forgetfulness. So it is established that it is by will. And the Mu'tazila do not affirm for God a meaning in will beyond knowledge without necessity after it was not, and this meaning is present in the action of every person in the world, so there is no basis for their denial of their own statement. And with God is protection. Then he said: Iblis's will is mere wish, and if the servants willed [faith] they would not disbelieve, and God has power to prevent them by compulsion. The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: We said to him: You have spoken truth; will necessitates coercion, but wish does not. So how did the wish of His enemy overcome His will? And his saying 'He has power and compels' — this type [of answer] is only the effect of confusion and alienation, and belief in compulsion is not permissible in any way. Then he said: If it is said: Do you see a wise man who has power to prevent his servant from a matter he does not will and does not prevent him? He objected with [the doctrine of] compulsion, and that is an error because according to us He wills it, and prevention is not a condition of what is willed. Then he said: He counts it for two aspects He does not will, and prevention is not permissible for Him due to some [aspect of] governance. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: If you were to measure by the witnessed, you would not find [such] except that he does not have power over it or he did not will the action. He said: Among [the cases] is that which necessitates prevention; so it indicates that if prevention is necessary, it is necessary for a cause, not for itself. What is mentioned of the cause, if it necessitated compulsion, then that is what was said: he does not have power over it. And if it does not necessitate, and he [the agent] may own compulsion without transgression, then it is not permissible for him according to us, and it is outside of custom. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a theological objection and its response regarding divine will and human action. The objector argues: most people disbelieve because Iblis willed it, yet God wills obedience from them. Thus Iblis's will appears more effective in God's own dominion. The author answers by distinguishing between will and emotions like pleasure and anger. A person can be pleased or angered without acting at that moment, but will is a condition for action; it must exist for the act to occur. Therefore, God does not love or have pleasure in the disbeliever as that would necessitate an action, whereas will is different. The author then states the common principle: action arises from will, coercion, or forgetfulness. God cannot be described by coercion or forgetfulness concerning the servant's act, so it must be by will. The Mu'tazila are criticized for not affirming a real attribute of will in God beyond a mere temporal knowledge without necessity. The text then presents a second objection: Iblis's will is mere wish (tamannī), not true will, because if the servants truly willed faith, they would not disbelieve. The jurist replies that will entails coercion (ghalaba), while wish does not, so how can the enemy's wish overcome God's will? Belief in compulsion (qahr) is rejected. A third objection asks: if a wise master can prevent his servant from an undesired act, why doesn't God do so? The opponent counters with compulsion, but this is wrong because God does will the act, and prevention is not required. The Shaykh explains that if one judges by human custom, prevention only occurs when the agent lacks power or does not will the act. Prevention, if necessary, must be for a cause, not arbitrarily. If the cause would lead to compulsion, then the agent truly lacks power; otherwise, compulsion is not permissible in divine governance. The passage concludes with a statement of reliance on God.

Key Terms
إرادة
غلبة
غفلة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God may act by coercion or be forgetful.
Correction: God is free from both; His actions are by will.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three possible origins of an action?
A) Will, power, and knowledge
B) Will, coercion, and forgetfulness
C) Desire, aversion, and indifference
D) Love, anger, and pleasure

Key Takeaway
Every human action occurs by God's will, not by coercion or forgetfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own actions, do you ever excusively attribute them to your own will, forgetting that they ultimately occur by God's will? How can you make the reality of His will more present in your daily life?
?
Have you ever felt that God's decree was forced upon you (coercion) or that He forgot about you (forgetfulness)? The lesson reminds us that God is not described by these. What steps can you take to trust in His perfect will even when you don't understand His plan?
?
The Mu'tazila reduced God's will to mere knowledge. Do you ever treat God's commands as just information to know, rather than a real will that demands your submission? What would change if you truly believed that every command is an expression of His will?

The Objection of Iblis's Will as Wish and the Nature of Prevention
Maturidi addresses the objection that Iblis's will is wish and the question of why God does not prevent disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi distinguishes between will and wish, and why God's ability to compel does not contradict His wisdom in allowing disbelief.

Core Idea
Iblis's will is mere wish; real will entails effective power.

A second objection arises: if Iblis's will is just a wish, why does it overcome God's will? Maturidi and the jurist respond by distinguishing will from wish, and then discuss the issue of divine prevention and compulsion. This lesson explores these nuanced arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection: Iblis's will is wish
Read the claim that Iblis's will is mere wish (tamannī), not true will.
2
Jurist's reply: will entails coercion
True will brings about its object; wish does not. So how does wish overcome God's will?
This turns the objection back on the opponent.
3
Analyze the objection about prevention
Why doesn't God prevent disbelief if He can?
4
Understand the response: prevention not required
God wills the act (for a wise purpose), and prevention is not a condition of what is willed.
The Shaykh's analysis shows prevention must be for a cause and not arbitrary.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's failure to prevent disbelief means He is powerless or approves.
Correction: God wills the act for a wise purpose, and prevention would entail compulsion, which is not part of divine governance.

Checkpoint
According to the jurist's reply, what distinguishes true will (إرادة) from mere wish (تمنى)?
A) Will is eternal, wish is temporal.
B) Will necessitates coercion (ghalaba), wish does not.
C) Will belongs to God, wish belongs to humans.
D) Will is a condition for action, wish is not.

Key Takeaway
True will is effective; divine prevention is not arbitrary but tied to wisdom and the nature of free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever silently ask, 'Why didn't God stop me?' What does this lesson teach you about your own responsibility and God's wisdom in allowing you to choose?
?
Iblis's will was mere wish—empty desire with no real resolve. Where in your life have you mistaken wishful thinking for true will? What would it mean for you to transform your wishes into effective will that aligns with God's guidance?
?
If you truly believed that God's prevention is not arbitrary but based on infinite wisdom, how would that change the way you react when suffering or evil befalls you? Will you now trust His governance even when you do not see the reason?

The Opponent's Misinterpretation of Divine Guidance
Maturidi reports the opponent's reinterpretation of Quran 6:125.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's argument that God's guidance is a reward for obedience, not an initial act, and their reasoning that it avoids divine partiality.

Core Idea
The opponent misconstrues divine guidance as a reward, not the means of guidance itself.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents an opponent's objection to the verse on divine guidance. The opponent argues that the expansion of the breast occurs after obedience, not before, to avoid the charge of divine favoritism. Let us examine their reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's argument
Read the Arabic passage where Maturidi reports the opponent's interpretation of the verse. Notice how the opponent claims the verse's meaning is 'known' and describes guidance as a reward for obedience.
2
Identify the verse and its reinterpretation
The opponent cites Quran 6:125 and reinterprets 'expansion of the breast' as a reward that God gives after a person obeys, not as the means of guidance.
3
Note the two reasons against initial guidance
The opponent gives two reasons why God cannot initiate expansion or narrowing without prior deserving: (1) God has no partiality or favoritism, and (2) if God distinguished between servants by mere letters, He could not blame them.
These reasons are meant to support the opponent's interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في جواب ما عورض بقوله : فمن يرد الله أن يهديه الله ، الآية : إن تأويله معروف، وهو أن من أطاعه آتاه من لطائفه ما لا يقدر عليه غيره، وسماه بالأسماء الشريفة، وحكم له بالأحكام الرفيعة ثوابًا لطاعته وليزداد منه الرغبة، كقوله : والذين اهتدوا زادهم هدى . ومن عصاه منع منه ما ذكر فيضيق صدره كما وصف، ولا يفعل بأحد ذلك ابتداء، كالآية التي ذكرتها ، وقوله : وما يضل به إلا الفاسقين . ثم قال : فلا يجوز ذلك ابتداء من غير استحقاق العداوة والولاية لأمرين أحدهما أن ليس به هوادة ولا محاباة. والثاني أن من يفرق بين عبيده بالحرف لم يكن له العود باللوم منهم على أحد. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : أما ما ادعى على الآية أنها معروفة فهذا يدل على جهله بالمعروف والمنكر، وقلبه القصة ثم أخطأ في صرف الآية إلى ما بعد الإسلام المعروف من النطق ، لأنه قال : فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام ، فأثبت له الإسلام إذ شرح صدره لا أن شرح بعد أن وجد منه الإسلام. ثم أعظم منه جرأته على الله أن مثل هذا يكون هوادة ومحاباة وما كان عليه ، إذ عُلِم مَن صفته جرأته هذه في خاص نفسه أن لا يُبدي ذلك ولا يعارض نفسه بما لا يُضطر إليه، لكنه عوقب بجهله بالله وصرفه كتابه عن جهته طلبا لإقامة مذهب هو ينتج الزندقة. فنعوذ بالله من الخذلان. ثم يقال: من أسلم وقت إسلامه أسلم وقلبه مشروح له و وقت كفره قلبه ضيق، أو هما واحد في الشرح
And he said in answer to what was objected with His saying: 'Whomsoever Allah wills to guide' [the verse]. He said: Its interpretation is known, and it is that whoever obeys Him, He gives him of His subtleties what no one else can give, and names him with noble names, and judges him with lofty judgments as a reward for his obedience, and so that he increases in desire [for it], like His saying: 'And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance' [47:17]. And whoever disobeys Him, He withholds from him what was mentioned, so his breast becomes narrow as described. And He does not do that to anyone initially, like the verse you mentioned, and His saying: 'And He misleads thereby only the defiantly disobedient' [2:26]. Then he said: So that [i.e., such treatment] is not permissible initially without deserving enmity and friendship for two reasons: one of them is that there is no partiality or favoritism in Him, and the second is that one who distinguishes between his servants by mere letters cannot then blame any of them. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: As for his claim about the verse being known, this indicates his ignorance of the known and the unknown, and he inverted the story and then erred in diverting the verse to after the known declaration of Islam, because he said: 'Whomsoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam' [6:125], so He attributed Islam to him when He expanded his breast, not that He expands after Islam occurs from him. Then greater than this is his audacity against God [in suggesting] that such [a thing] would be partiality and favoritism, and what was [the state] he was upon?! For it is known, from one whose description is this audacity in his own private self, that he would not manifest that nor oppose himself with what he is not compelled to, but he was punished with ignorance of God and turning His Book from its direction seeking to establish a school that produces heresy. So we seek refuge in God from abandonment. Then it is said: Whoever submits at the time of his submission, he submits while his heart is expanded for it, and at the time of his disbelief his heart is narrow, or both are one regarding expansion.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its refutation regarding the interpretation of Q. 6:125 ("Whomsoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam"). The opponent claims the verse is known to mean that after a person obeys, God gives subtleties and rewards, and that God does not initiate expansion or narrowing without prior deserving based on enmity or friendship, because God has no partiality and cannot blame servants for differentiation based on arbitrary favor ("mere letters"). The Shaykh (Imam Maturidi) refutes this: the opponent's claim of a "known" interpretation shows ignorance. The opponent misapplies the verse to after the verbal declaration of Islam (al-nuṭq), whereas the verse clearly states that God expands the breast *for* Islam, meaning the expansion is the cause of Islam, not the result. The Shaykh further condemns the opponent's audacity: suggesting that such divine action would be partiality or favoritism is worse, because the one who says this (the opponent) would not even himself act in such a contradictory manner unless compelled. The opponent is punished with ignorance and is seeking to establish a heretical doctrine (zandaqa). The passage ends with a clarification: at the moment of embracing Islam, the heart is expanded; at the moment of disbelief, it is narrow. The Shaykh questions whether expansion and narrowness are the same or distinct, leaving the matter open.

Key Terms
هداية
شرح الصدر
الضيق

Correction: The opponent argues that the verse refers to God's treatment after obedience/disobedience, not initial decree, to avoid implying divine favoritism. (Maturidi will refute this.)

A) Initially, before any human action
B) After a person obeys, as a reward
C) Only for prophets
D) At the time of creation

Key Takeaway
The opponent argues that the expansion of the breast is a reward for prior obedience, not a divine act initiating guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If guidance were truly a reward for obedience, would you be certain of your own guidance? What does this uncertainty teach you about relying on Allah's mercy and not your deeds?

Maturidi's Refutation of the Misinterpretation
Maturidi refutes the opponent's interpretation and rebukes their audacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's refutation of the opponent's misinterpretation, including his critique of their reversal of the verse's meaning and his condemnation of their audacity.

Core Idea
Maturidi exposes the opponent's error: the verse shows expansion precedes Islam, not the other way around.

Now Imam Maturidi directly refutes the opponent's claim. He points out their ignorance of the known meaning and their audacity in suggesting God's actions could be partiality. Let's follow his argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's critique
Read the Arabic passage from 'قال الشيخ رحمه الله' to the end. Note how Maturidi begins by rejecting the opponent's claim of a 'known' interpretation.
2
Understand the verse's sequence
Maturidi highlights that the verse says 'expands his breast for Islam' (li-l-islām), meaning the expansion is the cause of Islam, not a reward after it. The opponent reversed the order.
3
The gravity of the opponent's accusation
Maturidi condemns the opponent for suggesting that God's act of expanding the breast could be partiality or favoritism, calling it audacity and heresy.
4
Final clarification
The passage ends with a brief point about the state of the believer at the moment of submission: the heart is expanded, while the disbeliever's heart is narrow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في جواب ما عورض بقوله : فمن يرد الله أن يهديه الله ، الآية : إن تأويله معروف، وهو أن من أطاعه آتاه من لطائفه ما لا يقدر عليه غيره، وسماه بالأسماء الشريفة، وحكم له بالأحكام الرفيعة ثوابًا لطاعته وليزداد منه الرغبة، كقوله : والذين اهتدوا زادهم هدى . ومن عصاه منع منه ما ذكر فيضيق صدره كما وصف، ولا يفعل بأحد ذلك ابتداء، كالآية التي ذكرتها ، وقوله : وما يضل به إلا الفاسقين . ثم قال : فلا يجوز ذلك ابتداء من غير استحقاق العداوة والولاية لأمرين أحدهما أن ليس به هوادة ولا محاباة. والثاني أن من يفرق بين عبيده بالحرف لم يكن له العود باللوم منهم على أحد. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : أما ما ادعى على الآية أنها معروفة فهذا يدل على جهله بالمعروف والمنكر، وقلبه القصة ثم أخطأ في صرف الآية إلى ما بعد الإسلام المعروف من النطق ، لأنه قال : فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام ، فأثبت له الإسلام إذ شرح صدره لا أن شرح بعد أن وجد منه الإسلام. ثم أعظم منه جرأته على الله أن مثل هذا يكون هوادة ومحاباة وما كان عليه ، إذ عُلِم مَن صفته جرأته هذه في خاص نفسه أن لا يُبدي ذلك ولا يعارض نفسه بما لا يُضطر إليه، لكنه عوقب بجهله بالله وصرفه كتابه عن جهته طلبا لإقامة مذهب هو ينتج الزندقة. فنعوذ بالله من الخذلان. ثم يقال: من أسلم وقت إسلامه أسلم وقلبه مشروح له و وقت كفره قلبه ضيق، أو هما واحد في الشرح
And he said in answer to what was objected with His saying: 'Whomsoever Allah wills to guide' [the verse]. He said: Its interpretation is known, and it is that whoever obeys Him, He gives him of His subtleties what no one else can give, and names him with noble names, and judges him with lofty judgments as a reward for his obedience, and so that he increases in desire [for it], like His saying: 'And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance' [47:17]. And whoever disobeys Him, He withholds from him what was mentioned, so his breast becomes narrow as described. And He does not do that to anyone initially, like the verse you mentioned, and His saying: 'And He misleads thereby only the defiantly disobedient' [2:26]. Then he said: So that [i.e., such treatment] is not permissible initially without deserving enmity and friendship for two reasons: one of them is that there is no partiality or favoritism in Him, and the second is that one who distinguishes between his servants by mere letters cannot then blame any of them. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: As for his claim about the verse being known, this indicates his ignorance of the known and the unknown, and he inverted the story and then erred in diverting the verse to after the known declaration of Islam, because he said: 'Whomsoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam' [6:125], so He attributed Islam to him when He expanded his breast, not that He expands after Islam occurs from him. Then greater than this is his audacity against God [in suggesting] that such [a thing] would be partiality and favoritism, and what was [the state] he was upon?! For it is known, from one whose description is this audacity in his own private self, that he would not manifest that nor oppose himself with what he is not compelled to, but he was punished with ignorance of God and turning His Book from its direction seeking to establish a school that produces heresy. So we seek refuge in God from abandonment. Then it is said: Whoever submits at the time of his submission, he submits while his heart is expanded for it, and at the time of his disbelief his heart is narrow, or both are one regarding expansion.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its refutation regarding the interpretation of Q. 6:125 ("Whomsoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam"). The opponent claims the verse is known to mean that after a person obeys, God gives subtleties and rewards, and that God does not initiate expansion or narrowing without prior deserving based on enmity or friendship, because God has no partiality and cannot blame servants for differentiation based on arbitrary favor ("mere letters"). The Shaykh (Imam Maturidi) refutes this: the opponent's claim of a "known" interpretation shows ignorance. The opponent misapplies the verse to after the verbal declaration of Islam (al-nuṭq), whereas the verse clearly states that God expands the breast *for* Islam, meaning the expansion is the cause of Islam, not the result. The Shaykh further condemns the opponent's audacity: suggesting that such divine action would be partiality or favoritism is worse, because the one who says this (the opponent) would not even himself act in such a contradictory manner unless compelled. The opponent is punished with ignorance and is seeking to establish a heretical doctrine (zandaqa). The passage ends with a clarification: at the moment of embracing Islam, the heart is expanded; at the moment of disbelief, it is narrow. The Shaykh questions whether expansion and narrowness are the same or distinct, leaving the matter open.

Key Terms
الإسلام
المعروف
الزندقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the correct understanding of the verse 'He expands his breast for Islam'?
A) The expansion occurs after the person verbally declares Islam
B) The expansion is the cause of the person's submission to Islam
C) The expansion is a reward for previous good deeds
D) The expansion is metaphorical and has no real effect

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the opponent by showing that the expansion of the breast is the means of guidance, not a reward, and condemns the opponent for attributing partiality to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever read a verse of the Quran with a pre-formed opinion, twisting its meaning to fit your own desires? Will you repent and commit to seeking only what Allah intends, even if it contradicts your comfort?
?
Do you truly believe that every moment of guidance you experience is a pure gift from Allah—not because you deserved it, but because He chose to expand your heart? How will this reshape your gratitude and humility today?
?
When you see others who have not been guided, does it ever lead you to question Allah's justice or partiality? In light of this lesson, hold yourself accountable: will you trust in His perfect wisdom and refrain from judging His decree?

Refuting Claims of Favoritism in God's Actions
Maturidi refutes favoritism claims via dialectical questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses a structured dialectical argument to refute the claim that God's differential treatment of believers and disbelievers is arbitrary favoritism.

Core Idea
God's actions are not arbitrary but are the very basis for reward and punishment.

Imam Maturidi engages with an opponent who accuses God of favoritism for giving ease to believers and constriction to disbelievers. Through a series of logical questions, he exposes the incoherence of this claim and shows that such differences are essential to reward and punishment. Follow the steps of his dialectic closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the back-and-forth questioning style. This is a dialectical refutation.
The passage uses hypothetical questions to trap the opponent.
2
Identify the initial claim and refutation
The opponent first claims ease and constriction are the same. Maturidi says this is clearly false because everyone knows the difference between faith and disbelief.
This appeal to common knowledge is a strong move.
3
Follow the two branches of questioning
Maturidi asks two sets of questions: one about aid/difficulty in religion, and one about whether conversion is observed. Each branch forces the opponent into a contradiction.
Pay attention to the 'if yes, then...' and 'if no, then...' structure.
4
Understand the conclusion
The opponent's terms (favoritism, partiality) are rejected; what actually occurs is reward and punishment based on justice. The passage ends with a plea for protection from such error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والضيق ؟ فإن قال : كانا واحدا، ظهر كذبه عند كل من يحفظ ابتداء دينه من إسلام أو كفر. ثم يُسمي ما يعلم كذبه كل مسلم وكافر من الله هوادةً مرة ومحاباة أخرى، بائنا وصدا عن الحق، ومنعا ليعلموا جرأته وسفهه . ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يقال له : الذي يريده بعد الإيمان أو يحرمه بعد الكفر هل كان في ذلك معونة في الدين وتعسير عليه أو لا؟ فإن قال: لا، بان بهته وسقط موضع جعل ذلك ثوابًا أو عقابًا. وإن قال : بلى، فقد أقر على مذهبه بعدم بذل شيء هو أصلح له في الدين. ثم يقال: هل رأيت كافرًا بعد أن آمن، أو أُخبرت كون ذلك، أو مؤمنًا بعد الكفر ؟ لابد من: بلى. قيل: أكان إعطاء الثواب ومنعه ذلك الشرح أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، ألزمه الخلف في الوعد والكذبَ في الخبر. وإن قال: نعم، قيل: أي نفع له في تلك الفوائد، أو أي ضرر عليه في التضييق ؟ إذا ليجعل ذلك ثوابًا أو عقابًا ويمنع جواز ذلك ابتداء بما سمّاه مرة هوادة، ومرة محاباة، ومرة صدا، ومرة منعا . نسأل الله العصمة عن قول هذا عقباه.
And constriction? If he says: they were one, his falsehood appears to everyone who remembers the beginning of his religion, whether Islam or disbelief. Then he names what every Muslim and disbeliever knows to be false from God—favoritism (hawada) once and partiality (muḥabāt) another time, clear repulsion and turning away from truth, and prevention—so that they may know his audacity and foolishness. And there is no power except with Allah. Then it is said to him: That which He wills after faith or deprives after disbelief—was there in that assistance in religion and difficulty upon him or not? If he says: No, his slander becomes clear and the place of making that reward or punishment falls. If he says: Yes, then he has admitted according to his doctrine that He does not bestow anything that is more beneficial for him in religion. Then it is said: Have you seen a disbeliever after he believed, or have you been informed of that happening, or a believer after disbelief? Necessarily: Yes. It is said: Was the giving of reward and its prevention that expansion or not? If he says: No, he is bound by the breach of promise and lying in the report. If he says: Yes, it is said: What benefit is there for him in those benefits, or what harm upon him in constriction? So that He makes that reward or punishment and prevents the permissibility of that in the beginning by what He called once favoritism, once partiality, once repulsion, and once prevention. We ask Allah for protection from the consequence of this saying.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of an opponent (likely al-Ka'bi) who claims that God's actions of giving ease (sharḥ) or constriction (ḍīq) to believers and disbelievers are acts of favoritism or partiality. The argument proceeds through a series of questions and answers. First, if one claims that ease and constriction are the same, his falsehood is obvious because everyone recognizes the difference between faith and disbelief. Then the opponent is forced to admit that calling God's acts 'favoritism' contradicts what every Muslim and disbeliever knows—that such terms cannot apply to God. Next, the opponent is asked whether God's willing ease after faith and constriction after disbelief is an aid or a difficulty in religion. If he says it is not, then his claim falls apart because that would make reward and punishment meaningless. If he says it is, then he admits that God withholds what is more beneficial in religion, which contradicts his own doctrine. Further, the opponent is asked whether he has seen or heard of a disbeliever becoming a believer or a believer becoming a disbeliever. He must say yes. Then he is asked whether the giving or withholding of reward is that expansion or constriction. If he says no, he incurs breach of promise and lying. If he says yes, he is asked what benefit or harm there is in such benefits or constriction, concluding that these are actually reward and punishment and cannot be called favoritism. The passage ends with a plea for divine protection from such erroneous speech.

Key Terms
هوادة
محاباة
صدا
منع
شرح الصدر
ضيق الصدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's differential treatment of believers and disbelievers is arbitrary favoritism.
Correction: Maturidi shows it is based on justice and is precisely what makes reward and punishment meaningful.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the opponent says that God's giving ease or constriction is neither an aid nor a difficulty in religion?
A) He proves that God is just.
B) He admits that reward and punishment are meaningless.
C) He avoids slander.
D) He acknowledges God's favoritism.

Key Takeaway
God's granting ease to believers and constriction to disbelievers is not favoritism but the very basis of reward and punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that God was unfair to you, giving ease to others while constricting you? How does Maturidi’s argument that constriction is a form of punishment for disbelief force you to reexamine that feeling and your own spiritual state?
?
If you truly believed that every moment of spiritual expansion (sharḥ al-ṣadr) is a reward from God for your faith, and every constriction is a punishment for your disobedience, how would that change the way you respond to both? Would you still dare to complain or would you turn inward to examine your faith?
?
When you face difficulty in your faith, do you tend to accuse God of playing favorites or do you take responsibility? This passage says that denying the connection between constriction and punishment would be accusing God of breaking promises. What would it take for you to stop blaming God and start accounting for your own choices?

Refuting al-Ka'bi's Claim of Compulsion
Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's claim that divine will is compulsive force.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of al-Ka'bi's interpretation of Quranic verses that suggest divine will as compulsion, and why such a view undermines moral accountability.

Core Idea
Faith under compulsion is no faith at all—it strips praise and reward.

Al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili theologian, claimed that verses like Quran 10:99 indicate God's will as a compulsive force forcing belief. Maturidi counters that this interpretation is flawed because it misunderstands the nature of divine testing. In this lesson, we examine Maturidi's argument and its implications for human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Note the key terms: الإكراه (compulsion), القسر (force), مشيئة القسر (will of compulsion), الابتلاء (testing).
2
Identify al-Ka'bi's position
Al-Ka'bi interprets 'if your Lord had willed' as compulsion—that God could force everyone to believe by preventing disbelief. Find where Maturidi states this.
3
Understand Maturidi's counter-argument
Maturidi argues that God's will in these verses is about testing (ابتلاء), not compulsion. He cites another verse (47:4) and notes that the will of compulsion would entail no praise or reward.
4
Reflect on the theological stakes
Consider why this matters: if faith is compelled, it loses moral value. Maturidi's refutation upholds human responsibility and the meaningfulness of divine testing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في قوله تعالى ولو شاء ربك لآمن من في الأرض كلهم جميعًا إنه على الإكراه أن يمنعهم قسرًا كما جعلهم شيوخا وشبابًا، ولكن شاء أن يبتليهم، كقوله : ولو يشاء الله لانتصر منهم، وقد شاء ذلك بالنبي وأصحابه، ولكن أراد به مشيئة القسر، إذ ليس معها حمد ولا أجر. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : وقد بينا ما يدل على وهمه. على أنه من كان ممن سبق إلى قوله
And he said concerning His saying: 'And if your Lord had willed, all who are on the earth would have believed, all of them'—that it is upon compulsion, that He prevents them by force just as He made them old and young, but He willed to test them, like His saying: 'And if Allah willed, He would have taken vengeance upon them,' and He willed that for the Prophet and his companions, but He intended by it the will of compulsion, for there is no praise nor reward with it. The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: And we have already shown what indicates his error. And that he is one of those who preceded to his saying.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is Maturidi's refutation of al-Ka'bi's interpretation of Quran 10:99: 'And if your Lord had willed, all who are on the earth would have believed, all of them.' Al-Ka'bi claims that this verse refers to compulsion (ikrāh) or force (qasr), meaning that God could have forced everyone to believe by preventing them from disbelief, just as He made people old or young without their choice. However, Maturidi counters that God willed to test (yabtaliyahum) people, as indicated by the verse 'If Allah willed, He would have taken vengeance upon them' (47:4) and that He willed that for the Prophet and his companions, meaning that God's will regarding belief is not one of compulsion but of testing. The will of compulsion (mashī'at al-qasr) would entail no praise or reward for the believer, because belief under compulsion is not meritorious. Maturidi states that he has already shown the error of al-Ka'bi's view, and notes that al-Ka'bi follows a flawed precedent.

Key Terms
الإكراه
القسر
مشيئة القسر
الابتلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's will in verses like Quran 10:99 is a compulsive force that overrides human choice.
Correction: Maturidi explains that such verses refer to testing, not compulsion; compulsion would eliminate praise and reward, contradicting divine justice.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would be absent if God's will were a will of compulsion (mashī'at al-qasr)?
A) Reward and punishment.
B) The test itself.
C) Praise and reward.
D) Divine power.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the notion that divine will is coercive; true faith requires free choice and is a test, not a forced state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you sometimes wish God would simply force you to obey so you wouldn't have to struggle? Yet this lesson shows that such forced obedience carries no reward. What does that reveal about your desire for ease over genuine devotion?
?
The passage says there is no praise or reward with compelled faith. When you perform acts of worship, do you do them out of heartfelt praise for God or merely because you feel compelled? How would your worship change if you removed all external pressure?
?
Imagine if God made you old and young without your choice—compulsion. Your faith is not like that. In what area of your life are you treating your faith as if it were a compulsory fate rather than a voluntary test?

Abu Hanifa's Dialectical Argument on God's Knowledge and Will
Abu Hanifa's two-step argument against the Qadariyya on knowledge and will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hanifa's two-step logical argument that forces the Qadariyya to acknowledge God's comprehensive will based on His foreknowledge.

Core Idea
God's knowledge of the future logically entails His will for all events.

This passage presents a classic dialectical argument by Imam Abu Hanifa against the Qadariyya, who denied divine predestination. Using a simple two-question dilemma, he forces them to either accept God's full knowledge and will or fall into disbelief and attributing ignorance to God. The argument is a model of concise theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to understand the flow of the argument. Notice the two questions and the possible responses.
Pay attention to the logical consequences drawn from each answer.
2
Identify the two points of discussion
The passage mentions 'two points' (حرفين). Identify what they are: the first is about God's knowledge, the second about His will. See how they are connected.
The second point only arises if the opponent answers 'yes' to the first.
3
Trace the logical implications
For each possible answer, note the consequence: denying knowledge leads to disbelief; affirming knowledge but denying will leads to attributing ignorance to God; affirming both leads to acceptance of qadar.
This shows the argument forces the Qadariyya into a corner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله: بيننا وبين القدرية الكلام في حرفين. أن نسألهم: هل علم الله ما يكون أبداً على ما يكون؟ فإن قالوا لا كفروا، لأنهم جهلوا ربهم. وإن قالوا: نعم قيل: شاء أن ينفذ علمه كما علم أو لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، قالوا بأن الله شاء أن يكون جاهلاً، ومن شاء ذلك فليس بحكيم. وإن قالوا نعم أقروا بأنه شاء أن يكون كل شيء كما علم أن يكون فهذا الذي تقرر عندي من المحكي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، لا أني ذكرته بلفظه. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, said: Between us and the Qadariyya is discussion on two points. We ask them: Did God know what will come to be forever as it will be? If they say no, they disbelieve because they have ignored their Lord. And if they say yes, it is said: Did He will to execute His knowledge as He knew or not? If they say no, they say that God willed to be ignorant, and whoever wills that is not wise. And if they say yes, they acknowledge that He willed everything to be as He knew it would be. This is what I have established from what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, not that I mentioned it in his wording. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument attributed to Abu Hanifa against the Qadariyya, who deny divine predestination. It presents a logical dilemma: either God knows the future or not. If they deny His knowledge, that implies ignorance, which is disbelief. If they affirm His knowledge, then either He wills events to occur as He knows them or He wills the opposite. If they say He wills the opposite, that means He wills ignorance, which is unwise. If they say He wills as He knows, then they must admit that God wills all things to happen exactly as He knows, which establishes predestination. The argument is concise and uses a two-step questioning to force the opponent into affirming God's comprehensive will.

Key Terms
علم
إرادة
قدرية
حكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Qadariyya can affirm God's knowledge but still deny His will without inconsistency.
Correction: The argument shows that if God knows something will happen and does not will it, then His knowledge would be contrary to reality, which implies ignorance. Thus affirming knowledge logically requires affirming will.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, if the Qadariyya say God did not know the future, what is the consequence?
A) They become ignorant
B) They disbelieve because they are ignorant of their Lord
C) They are excused because knowledge is not necessary
D) They must affirm that God willed the opposite

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's argument forces the Qadariyya to accept that God's knowledge entails His will, thereby establishing the reality of divine predestination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God knows every choice you will make today, including the sinful ones? If He knows and still wills it to happen, how does that change your view of your own responsibility and His mercy?
?
When you face a calamity or a failure, do you submit to God's decree, or do you secretly resent that He allowed it? Can you honestly say, 'I believe God knew this would happen and willed it for my good'?
?
Have you ever acted as though you know better than God—by worrying about the future or by trying to control outcomes that are already in His knowledge and will? What would it look like to surrender that control today?

Al-Qada': Its Linguistic Reality and Connection to Creation
Maturidi defines al-qada' and establishes its connection to the creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Islamic concept of al-qada' (divine decree) encompasses multiple meanings including creation, judgment, and informing, and is fundamentally linked to the creation of actions.

Core Idea
Al-qada' is not just predestination; it is God's wise judgment and creation of all things.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi lays the groundwork for understanding al-qada' and al-qadar. He begins by connecting the issue to the creation of actions, then provides a detailed linguistic analysis of the word 'qada''. As you read, notice how Maturidi uses Quranic verses to support each shade of meaning, showing that al-qada' is a rich concept with both creative and judicial dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage starts with a general statement before getting into the definition.
2
Identify the core thesis
Maturidi states that this issue is rooted in the creation of actions. Ask yourself why that connection is essential for understanding qada' and qadar.
The creation of actions is the foundation upon which qada' and qadar are built.
3
Analyze the definitions of qada'
The passage gives multiple meanings: judgment/decisive determination, creation, and informing. Find each one and note the Quranic verses used to support them.
Each meaning is tied to a specific Quranic usage.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how these definitions affect our understanding of divine decree and human action. How do the different meanings interact?
This reflection helps integrate the lesson into broader theological discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في القضاء والقدر

الأصل عندنا أن هذه المسألة ومسألة الإرادة كلها في خلق الأفعال، إن ثبت ذلك ثبتت هذه، إذ خلق الأفعال يثبت القضاء بكونها والقدر لها على ما عليها من حسن وقبح، ويوجب أن يكون مريدا لها أن تكون خلقا له. وقد بينا في هذا ما نرجو به الكفاية لمن أكرم بالهداية. لكن الناس أفردوا التكلم في مسألة منها فاتبعناهم في الفعل، لما احتمل أن يكونوا أرادوا أن الحق قد يظهر بنوره لمن تأمل بأي لفظ من الألفاظ يعبر به عنه، ليعلم أن الحق لا صار حقا للسان ولا لنوع من البيان، لكن صار حقا بما له من الأدلة والبراهين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.

ثم «القضاء» في حقيقته الحكم بالشيء والقطع على ما يليق به وأحق أن يقطع عليه». فرجع مرة إلى خلق الأشياء، لأنه تحقيق كونها على ما هي عليه، وعلى الأولى بكل شيء أن يكون على ما خلق؛ إذ الذي خلق الخلق هو الحكيم العليم؛ والحكمة هي إصابة الحقيقة لكل شيء ووضعه موضعه. قال الله تعالى : فقضاهن سبع سموات، الآية. وعلى ذلك يجوز وصف أفعال الخلق أن قضى بهن أي خلقهن وحكم بهن كقوله: فاقض ما أنت قاض بمعنى احكم. ومن ثمة سمي العالم قاضيا بما يرد كل حق إلى محقه ويبين الذي هو حق ذلك؛ وكذا قوله : إذا قضى أمرا فإنما يقول له كن فيكون. وكذلك يجوز أن يقال: حكم الله أن فلانا يفعل كذا في وقت كذا، فيكون منه كذا في وقت كذا. وحق هذا أن يكون حكم بما علم أنه يكون، وحكم أيضا بالذي يستحق الفاعل بفعله من ذم أو مدح، ثواب أو عقاب. و «قضى» أي أعلم وأخبر، كقوله : وقضينا إلى بني إسرائيل، الآية، وعلى هذا الوجه
A Question on al-Qada' and al-Qadar

The basis with us is that this question and the question of will are entirely about the creation of actions. If that is established, this is established. For the creation of actions establishes al-qada' (decree) of them being, and al-qadar (measure) for them according to what they are of good and evil, and necessitates that He be willing for them to be as His creation. We have already explained in this what we hope is sufficient for those honored with guidance. But people have separately spoken about one question from them, so we followed them in the action, because it is possible that they intended that the truth may appear by its light to whoever reflects by any wording from among the wordings expressed about it, so that it is known that truth did not become true due to the tongue nor due to a type of expression, but it became true due to what it has of proofs and evidences. And there is no power except with God.

Then 'al-qada'' in its reality is judgment (al-hukm) concerning something and decisive determination upon what is befitting it and most deserving to be decided upon. So it sometimes refers back to the creation of things, because it is the realization of their being as they are, and it is most appropriate for everything to be as it was created; for the One who created creation is the Wise, the Knowing; and wisdom is hitting the reality of each thing and placing it in its place. God Almighty said: 'So He completed them as seven heavens' (Surah Fussilat 41:12), the verse. And upon that, it is permissible to describe the actions of creation that He 'qada' (decreed) them, i.e., He created them and judged them, as His saying: 'So judge what you will judge' (Surah Ta-Ha 20:72) meaning 'decide'. And from that the scholar is called a judge (qadi) because he returns every right to its due and clarifies what is the right of that. And likewise His saying: 'When He decrees a matter, He only says to it "Be," and it is' (Surah Al 'Imran 3:47). And likewise it is permissible to say: God judged that so-and-so does such-and-such at such time, and such-and-such occurs from him at such time. And the truth of this is that He judged according to what He knew would be, and He also judged according to what the doer deserves by his action of blame or praise, reward or punishment. And 'qada' means He informed and told, as His saying: 'And We decreed to the Children of Israel' (Surah Al-Isra 17:4), the verse. And upon this aspect...
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage introduces the issue of al-qada' and al-qadar. The author states that this issue, along with the issue of divine will, revolves around the creation of actions. If the creation of actions is established, then qada' and qadar are established, because the creation of actions affirms that God decrees their existence and measures them as good or evil, and that He wills them as His creation. The author then notes that people have treated this as a separate question, and he follows them in doing so, because the truth can be expressed in various wordings; truth does not depend on language but on proofs. Next, he defines 'al-qada'' linguistically as judgment (hukm) and decisive determination (qat') upon what is fitting. This term can refer to creation, as when God says 'So He completed them as seven heavens' meaning He created them. It can also refer to judgment, as in 'So judge what you will judge' meaning decide. Hence, the scholar is called a qadi because he returns each right to its proper place. The term also appears in the verse 'When He decrees a matter, He only says to it "Be," and it is.' Additionally, it is permissible to say that God judged that a certain person will do such-and-such at a certain time, and it will happen accordingly. This judgment is based on His knowledge of what will be, and also includes judgment of what the doer deserves in terms of blame or praise, reward or punishment. Finally, 'qada' can mean informing, as in 'And We decreed to the Children of Israel.' The passage ends with 'and upon this aspect,' indicating a continuation.

قدر (qadar)
خلق الأفعال (khalq al-af'al)
حكم (hukm)
قطع (qat')

Misconception: Some think al-qada' only means predestination without distinction.
Correction: Maturidi shows it has multiple meanings including creation, judgment, and informing, all rooted in God's wisdom.

Meanings of Qada Attributable to God
Maturidi distinguishes permissible and impermissible meanings of qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different meanings of the term 'qada' when attributed to God and which are permissible or impermissible.

Core Idea
Not all meanings of 'qada' apply to God; only command and informing are valid.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi clarifies a crucial theological nuance: the term 'qada' (decree) can have different meanings, and not all can be attributed to God. He distinguishes permissible meanings (informing, command in good things) from impermissible ones (completion implying temporal change). This distinction protects God's transcendence while affirming His decree.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The passage discusses the word 'qada' and its attribution to God. Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall flow.
Notice that Maturidi starts with a permissible meaning before moving to others.
2
Identify the three meanings
List the three meanings Maturidi presents: informing, command, and finishing/completion. Pay attention to how each is introduced.
They are introduced with phrases like 'يرجع إلى الخبر', 'قد يكون أمر', 'وقد يكون في معنى فرغ'
3
Note the ruling for each
For each meaning, determine whether it is permissible to attribute to God and under what conditions. Refer to the commentary for clarification.
The meaning of 'command' is restricted to good things.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Ask why Maturidi makes these distinctions. How does this protect God from anthropomorphic qualities?
This lesson guards against attributing temporal, changeable actions to God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أيضاً يجوز أن يضاف إلى الله وهو يرجع إلى الخبر بما علم جل ثناؤه، ولا تمانع في جواز ذلك. وقضى قد يكون أمر، كقوله تعالى: وقضى ربك ألا تعبدوا إلا إياه، وقوله: وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة إذا قضى الله ورسوله أمرا، وهذا لا يجوز أن يضاف إلى الله إلا في الخيرات. وقد يكون في معنى فرغ كقوله: فلما قضى موسى الأجل، لكن هذا النوع لا يجوز أن يضاف إلى الله، لإضافة الشغل له بشيء أو فراغ له منه، إلا على مجاز اللغة في تحقيق انقضاء ما خلق ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقد ذكر غير هذا في القضاء مما ليس بنا إلى ذكره حاجة فيما نحن فيه.
Also, it is permissible to attribute [qada] to God, and it refers to [His] informing of what He knows—glory be to Him—and there is no impediment to permitting that. And 'qada' can be a command, as His saying: 'And your Lord has decreed (qada) that you not worship except Him,' and His saying: 'It is not for a believing man or a believing woman, when God and His Messenger have decreed (qada) an affair...'—this is not permissible to attribute to God except in good things. And it can be in the sense of 'finished,' as His saying: 'When Moses completed (qada) the term'—but this type is not permissible to attribute to God, because it implies occupation with something or freedom from it, except metaphorically in language to denote the completion of what He creates. And there is no power except with God. And other [meanings] have been mentioned concerning qada which we have no need to mention in what we are discussing.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage defines the permissible and impermissible meanings of the term 'qada' (decree/command) when attributed to God. The author begins by stating that 'qada' can be attributed to God when it refers to His informing of what He knows—there is no objection to that. He then notes that 'qada' can mean 'command,' citing Quranic verses: 'And your Lord has decreed that you not worship except Him' and the verse about God and His Messenger decreeing an affair. However, this use is only permissible when the decree concerns good things. Next, the author distinguishes another meaning: 'qada' can mean 'to finish' or 'to complete,' as in 'When Moses completed the term.' This meaning, however, cannot be attributed to God in a literal sense because it implies that God is occupied with something or becomes free from it—both are anthropomorphic. It can only be used metaphorically to indicate the completion of creation. The author concludes by noting that other meanings of 'qada' exist but are not relevant to the present discussion. The passage carefully guards against misattributing temporal properties to God while affirming that God's decree is a matter of His knowledge and command.

أمر (command)
فراغ (completion)
خبر (informing)

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Maturidi clarifies that when attributed to God, 'qada' primarily means command or decree, not completion in a temporal sense.

Two Meanings of Qadr and Their Divine Origin
Maturidi classifies qadr into two faces and proves both are from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two distinct meanings of qadr in Maturidi's theology and why both are proven to originate from Allah alone.

Core Idea
Qadr has two faces: the precise nature of creation and its specific circumstances—both come only from God.

Maturidi begins by distinguishing two meanings of 'qadr' (divine measure/destiny). First, it refers to the exact limit and quality given to each created thing. Second, it refers to the specific time, place, and outcome of events. He then argues that both aspects are beyond human capacity and therefore must be from God. This passage establishes the foundational understanding of predestination in the Maturidi school.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then consult the English translation. Notice the key terms like 'قدر', 'حد', 'خلق'.
2
Identify the two meanings
Maturidi explicitly says qadr has two aspects. Find the first (الحد الذي عليه يخرج الشي) and the second (بيان ما عليه يقع كل شيء). Write them down in your own words.
The first is about the inherent nature/quality of a thing; the second is about its spatiotemporal context and consequences.
3
Examine the proofs
For the first meaning, note the argument: creatures' actions exhibit qualities beyond their imagination and intellect, proving these measures come from God. For the second, note that the timing and location of actions are beyond human knowledge, so they too must be from God.
The proofs are based on human incapacity to fully determine or know these aspects.
4
Connect to scripture and hadith
The author references the Quranic verse 'إنا كل شيء خلقناه بقدر' and the hadith of Gabriel about belief in qadr. See how these support the classification.
The hadith explicitly links qadr's good and evil to God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القدر فهو على وجهين أحدهما الحد الذي عليه يخرج الشي، وهو جعل كل شيء على ما هو عليه من خير أو شر، من حسن أو قبح من حكمة أو سفه، وهو تأويل الحكمة أن يجعل كل شيء على ما هو عليه، ويصيب في كل شيء الأولى به؛ وعلى مثل هذا قوله: إنا كل شيء خلقناه بقدر. والثاني بيان ما عليه يقع كل شيء من زمان ومكان، وحق وباطل وما له من الثواب والعقاب. وعلى مثل أحد هذين المروي عن رسول الله عند سؤال جبريل عليه السلام إياه عن الإيمان أن قرن ما ذكرنا بالقدر خيره وشره من الله. فالأول - نحو خلق الشيء على ما هو عليه ـ قائم ذلك في أفعال الخلق: من خروجها على ما لا يبلغه أوهامهم من الحسن و القبح ولا يقدرها عقولهم، فثبت أنها خرجت على ذلك بالله سبحانه. والثاني أيضاً لا يحتمل منهم تقدير أفعالهم من الزمان والمكان ولا يبلغه علمهم. فمن ذلك الوجه أيضاً لا يحتمل أن تكون بهم، وهي غير خارجة عن الله، وقال الله تعالى: وقدرنا فيها السير، الآية، وقال: وإلا امرأته قدرنا إنها لمن الغابرين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
As for qadr (measure/destiny), it has two aspects: one is the limit upon which a thing emerges, and it is the placing of everything as it is, whether good or evil, beautiful or ugly, wise or foolish—it is the interpretation of wisdom: that He places everything as it is, and hits in everything what is most appropriate for it. And like this is His saying: 'Indeed, all things We created with qadr (measure).' The second is the clarification of how everything occurs in terms of time and place, truth and falsehood, and what it has of reward and punishment. And upon one of these two is the narration from the Messenger of God when Gabriel asked him about faith: that he (the Prophet) associated what we mentioned with qadr, its good and evil from God. So the first—like the creation of a thing as it is—is established in the actions of creatures: in their emerging in a way that their imaginations cannot reach in terms of beauty and ugliness, nor do their intellects measure them. So it is proven that they emerged thus by God, exalted is He. The second also cannot be borne by them—the estimation of their actions in terms of time and place—nor does their knowledge reach it. Thus from that aspect also it cannot be that they [do it], and they are not outside of God. And God Almighty said: 'And We measured (qaddarna) the journey stages therein'—the verse—and said: 'Except his wife; We decreed (qaddarna) that she would be among those who remain behind.' And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage classifies the term 'qadr' (divine measure/destiny) into two distinct meanings and argues that both are from God, not from creatures. The author first states that 'qadr' has two aspects. The first is the limit or measure upon which every thing is created—that God makes each thing exactly as it is in terms of good or evil, beauty or ugliness, wisdom or foolishness. This is described as the 'interpretation of wisdom,' meaning God precisely assigns to each thing what is most fitting. The Quranic verse 'Indeed, all things We created with qadr' supports this. The second aspect is the manifestation of how each thing occurs: its time, place, truth or falsehood, and the reward or punishment associated with it. The author then references the famous hadith of Gabriel, where faith includes belief in qadr, its good and evil from God. Next, Maturidi proves that the first aspect—the specific nature of creation—is evident in the actions of creatures: their actions emerge with such precise qualities of beauty or ugliness that human imagination and intellect cannot grasp them fully, proving that these qualities are bestowed by God. Similarly, the second aspect—the precise timing and location of actions—is beyond human knowledge and capacity, so it too must come from God. Thus both meanings of qadr are entirely from God, and creatures cannot independently determine them. The passage concludes with Quranic examples of God's measuring.

Key Terms
قدر (qadr)
حد (limit)
خلق (creation)
بيان (manifestation)
أفعال الخلق (actions of creatures)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'qadr' refers only to a general predetermination without specific details.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that qadr has two specific meanings: the precise measure of each thing's nature (its qualities) and the specific circumstances of its occurrence (time, place, etc.), both from God.

Checkpoint

A) Creatures can perfectly measure their own actions
B) The actions of creatures exhibit qualities beyond human imagination and intellect
C) The hadith of Gabriel explicitly states it
D) The Quran mentions it in the story of Moses

Key Takeaway
The two meanings of qadr—the specific nature of each thing and its precise circumstances—are both entirely from Allah, affirming divine omnipotence and human dependence.

?
